COMMISSIONERS
PROPOSED RESOLUTION
Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by
HERBERT T. SCHUMANN, JR., County Commiss ioner
PROPOSED RESOLUTION
Amending the Resolution Regarding the Regulation of Signs
Approved and Adopted January 20, 1999
Whereas, the regul ation and zoning control of signs in the unincorporated areas of Cook County
were adopted 6Â¥ef almost twenty-five years ago; and
Whereas, numerous conflicts have developed over the years between the growth and development
of the unincorporated areas and areas under municipal authority, and the proliferation of signs,
particularly large advertising signs; and
Whereas, s igns permitted under the 1976 Cook County Zoning Ordinance are now considered out
of place, particularly in areas attempting to preserve scenic and aesthetic assets; and
Whereas, a comprehensive amendment to Article 12 of the Cook County Zoning Ordinance has
been proposed and introduced for consideration by the Cook County Board of Commissioners; and
Whereas, the proposed amendments have been referred to the Committee on Zoning for public
hearing and comment, which process +s was expected to take several months to complete; and
Whereas, these proposed sign regulations have yet to be considered by the Committee on Zoning
and Building; and
Whereas, the proposed sign regulations will substantially amend the s ize and location permitted
for many signs, and will make certain signs non-conforming subject to amortization and removal; and
Whereas, the ongoing isst:Janee of bHilding permits and/or zoning relief 1:Jnder the e>dsting zoning
ordinanee 1:Jndermines the ability of Cook County to effeetively regt:Jlate the proliferation of eontlieting
signs thro1:Jgho1:Jt the 1:Jnineorporated areas of Cook Cot:Jnty.
Whereas the moratorium on the iss uance of permits for advertising signs has been effective in
limiting the proliferation of adve1tising signs, however, bus inesses in unincorporated Cook County are
seeking zoning relief for the replacement and modernization of on premi ses advertising signs;
NOW THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED AS FOLLOWS:
From the date of adoption of this Resolution and until review of the comprehensive amendment
I.
to Article 12 of the Cook County Zoning Ordinance has been completed, there shall be a moratorium on
the issuance of any and all permits for the construction, expansion or relocation of all signs or for zoning
relief as regulated by Article 12 of the 1976 Cook County Zoning Ordinance.

1765

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 15, 200 I
2.
The Commissioner of Building and Zoning shall, upon sufficient evidence submitted by an
app licant, have the authority to issue a permit fo r replacement of s ign(s)located on and within the
premises of a business or property owner where such sign(s)existed prior to the moratorium and which
have come into disrepair due to damage by weather conditions, accident, intentional acts of vandalism, eF
in instances where the business at which the existing sign is located has changed, or in instances in which
the property or business owner deems that an existing on premises sign no longer appropriately projects
the quality of the business and where, due to the age and deterioration of construction materials used,
such sign(s) detract from the value of the business property. The issuance of a permit fo r the replacement
of previously existing signs shall be only fo r restricted to applications for those on premises signs oot
reqlliring a Yariation f'rorn , and that meet the req uirements of, the 1976 Cook County Zoning Ordinance.
3.
The Commissioner of Bui lding and Zoning shall take appropriate steps to inform the Zoning
Administrator and the Zoning Board of Appeals of this relief under the moratorium.
4.
If, upon the expiration of six months from the date of adoption of this amended moratorium ,
review of the proposed amend ments to Article 12 has not been concluded, the this amended moratorium
hereby imposed shall be reviewed and the County Board shall determine whether a basis exists to extend
the moratorium for a further period of time.

Commissioner Hansen, seconded by Commissioner Schumann, moved to suspend the rules so that this
matter may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.
Commissioner Schumann, seconded by Commissioner Sutker, moved that the comm unication be referred
to the Committee on Zoning and Building. (Comm. No. 243595). The motion carried unanimously.

requesting authorization to receive from the federal Department of Labor, through the lllinois Department

CONTRACT
Transmitting a Communication from
RUTH M. ROTHSTEIN, Chief, Bureau of Health Services
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to enter into a contract with the Illinois Hospital and
HealthSystems Association, Naperville, Illinois, to license its COMPdata services.
Reason:

The contract will permit licensing online access to COMPdata for all three Bureau of Health
Services hospitals: Cook County Hospital , Oak Forest Hospital of Cook County and
Provident Hospital of Cook County.
COMPdata is a data product utilized by nearly all Illinois hospitals. Joint Commission
accreditation procedures now require quarterly electronic submittal of "ORYX" quality
indicators by an outside agency. COMPdata wi ll provide this information to the Joint
Commission, and thereby ass ist the Bureau of Health Services in its accreditation process and
its ongoing quality management activities.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: $54,000.00. Contract period: July I, 200 I through June 30, 2002. (897-880
Account). Requisition No. 18970772.
The Chief Information Officer has reviewed this item and concurs with this recommendation.

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Steele, moved that the County Purchasing Agent
be authorized to enter into the requested contract. The motion carried unanimously.

RESOLUTION
APPROPRIATING RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, there is an increasing need for pavement improvements to County highways in the City
of Chicago; and
WHEREAS, the County Highway Department does not have the manpower to design and prepare
plans or provide construction inspection, in a timely manner, at all the locations requiring improvements.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that an outside Consulting Engineer be contracted, with
review and supervision by County forces, to perform the design engineering, contract and plan
preparation and construction inspection services for highway improvements at various locations under
County jurisdiction in the City of Chicago; and

1792

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 15, 200 I
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the services as proposed shall consist of: preparation of
reports, plans, special provisions, permits and estimates for resurfacings, pavement rehabilitations,
viaduct clearance improvements, signalizatio ns, streetscapings and other highway improvements;
providing constructio n inspecti on services including resident engineering, material testing, survey, and
project documentation; and, said services shall be designated as Sectio n: 01-8DECC-O 1-ES MFT; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that there is hereby appropriated the sum of Seven Hundred
Thousand and No/I 00 Dollars, ($700,000.00) from the County's allotment of Motor Fuel Tax Funds for
the funding of this contract; and
BE IT FURTH ER RESOLVED, that the C lerk is hereby directed to transmit two certified copies of
this resolution to the district office of the Department of Transportation.

approved and adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

paid from the Workmen's Compensation Fund.

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 15, 2001
Ladies and Gentlemen:
Your Committee on Construction of the Board of Commissioners of Cook County met pursuant to notice
on Friday, May 4, 200 I at the hour of I 0:30 AM in the Board Room, Room 569, County Building, 118
North Clark Street, Chicago, Illinois.
Your Committee has considered the followi ng items and upon adoption of this report, the
recommendations are as follows:

Commissioner Moreno, seconded by Commissioner Butler, moved to suspend the rules so that Item
236803 may be considered. The motion carried.
236803

OFFICE OF CAPITAL PLANNING AND POLICY, by Michael E. LaMont, Director,
transmitting a Comm unication dated June 9, 2000:
Transmitted herewith for your approval is a request for authorization for the Purchasing
Agent to advertise for bids for Rockwell Warehouse Renovation: Phase II - Interior. It is
respectfully requested that thi s honorable body approve this request.
This project involves the upgrade/replacement of mechanical and e lectrical systems,
plumbing and sprinkler systems, and life safety systems.
Bond Issue (20000 Account).
Sufficient fu nds have been appropriated to cover this request.

*Referred to the Construction Committee on 6/20/00.
*Deferred at the Construction Meeting of 6/28/00.
Chairman Carr asked Michael LaMont to give a brief explanation in regards to the supplemental item.
Michael LaMont stated that the s upplemental item is for the interior upgrade of the mechanical-e lectrical
system at the Rockwell Warehouse. In June 2000, the Office of Capital Planning and Policy asked for
approval to advertise for bids for the upgrade, but studies of the electrical system were being conducted at
the time the request came before the committee. Mr. LaMont said he then req uested that the item be
deferred in comm ittee until the studies were completed. He said the initial request was less of an upgrade,
but now a more extensive upgrade of the electrical and mechanical systems is being requested. He
commented that it was believed the switchgear and electrical distribution panels could be reused,
however, the decision was made to replace them.
Mr. LaMont informed the committee that the boiler system dates back to the I 920's and also needs to be
replaced. A new stand-alone boiler room wi ll be built, which will be more cost efficient. He stated that
when the Office of Capital Planning and Policy received the recommendations from the consultant, he
realized there was not enough appropriation in the bond account so the decision was made to wait until
the Capital Budget for fiscal year 200 I could be amended.

Commissioner Moreno, seconded by Vice Chairman Butler, moved to approve Communication No.
236803. The motion carried.
Commissioner Collins voted present on the above item.

*Referred to the Construction Committee on 5/1/01.
Michael LaMont explained that there are two items re lated to building out the data center at the New
Cook County Hospital, the one that is before the committee today and a previous one that is
Communication number 243249. He explained that in building out the data center there are two
components, the data center itself which is a room of approximately 6,000 square feet in the hospital
building and consists of all the networking equipment, the floor and the environmental controls that are
being bid. He further stated that Communication number 243254 involves getti ng the proper power to the
data center room. The data center room has specialized power requirements that are over and above what
the hospital can handle. He also stated that when the architect began with the design of the hospital in
1996, there was no budget approved, plan or layout exactly for a data center because it was too early to
begin that type of planning, however, space was identified fo r the data center. Once the design proceeded
and the electrical loadings were defined, Unisource Network Systems looked at the amount of power
coming out of the new power plant and determined there was not sufficient power. He said he is
requesting authorization for Unisource Network Systems to bring the necessary normal and emergency
power from the new power plant into the data room .
Mr. LaMont said the reason the Office of Capital Planning and Policy is requesting a contract
modification is that the equipment needed to bring the power to the substations, switch gear and transfer
switches must be compatible with existing hospital equipment. He stated that if the County wou ld go to
bid, the cost would be more because the County may have to bring on new contractors who are unfamiliar
with the equipment, the plant and existing warranties may be voided.

WHEREAS, Evergreen Park Mayor Anthony Vacco has had a lifelong and distinguished career in public
service; and

WHEREAS, Anthony Vacco has served Evergreen Park as Building and Zoning Chairman ( 196 1-1 965),
as Trustee (I 965- I 968) and was appointed mayor in October I 968. He was elected to his first full fo uryear term in I 969, and has been re-elected in each successive mayoral election s ince then, accumu lating a

Village of Evergreen Park, and indeed the whole southwest region of Cook County, has flourished and
prospered; and

WHEREAS, throughout his long tenure as Mayor and Village President, Anthony Vacco has a lways
been a steadfast and stalwart advocate for the people of his community and the people of Cook County.
In addition to his mayoral responsibilities he has been elected to and appointed to leadership pos itions in
the National League of Cities, the Illinois Municipal League, Cook County Solid Waste Disposal

BOBBIE L. STEELE AND CALVIN R. SUTKER, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, Save A Life Foundation, founded in 1992, strives to provide training in the uniform
and safe application of basic life-supporting first aid skills to all those who may become involved in
attempting to aid people in need of such measures; and
WHEREAS, Save A Life Foundation offers (i) invaluable programs for children and students
("Save A Life for Kids" for students from the ages of 4 through 12 and " Bystander Basics" for high
school students) in recognition and appropriate responses to emergency situations, and (ii) training and
continuing education for police officers in basic life-saving emergency skills; and
WHEREAS, the efforts of Save A Life Foundation and its founder, Carol J. Spizzirri, were
instrumental in the enactment of a law (signed by Governor Edgar in September 1994) requiring police
officers and firefighters to be trained in first aid and CPR prior to graduating from their academies; and
WHEREAS, the week of May 20-26, 2001, has been proclaimed Save A Life Week (in
conjunction with EMS Week) by the Honorable George H. Ryan, Governor of the State of lllinois; and
WHEREAS, this Body takes great pride in recognizing those citizens of this County and
organizations which have made positive contributions for the better of our society .
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County
does hereby join in recognizing the week of May 20-26, 2001 , as Save A Life Week and does hereby
designate the week of May 20-26, 200 I, as Save A Life Week in Cook County; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does hereby
commend Save A Life Foundation and its board members, officers, staff, instructors, and volunteers for
their good work and dedicated service in helping others and saving lives; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that suitable copies of this Resolution be tendered to Save A Life
Foundation and its President/CEO/Founder, Carol J. Spizzirri, as recognition of their good work and
public service and also spread upon the official proceedings of this Honorable Body .

WHEREAS, Father Gino Dalpiaz, C.S., will celebrate his 50th Anniversary of priestly ordination on
June 24 2001 , at a Solemn Mass of Thanksgiving at Our Lady of Mount Carmel Church in Melrose Park
and at a banquet in his honor at the Alta Villa; and
WHEREAS, Father Dalpiaz was born in Melrose Park, the eldest often children of Firmino and Gelinda
Dalpiaz, and attended Sacred Heart Seminary. In 1947 he was sent to Rome, Italy, for graduate and
postgraduate studies in philosophy and theology; and

1894

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 15, 200 I
WHEREAS, Father Dalpiaz was ordained in Rome on July 8, 1951; and
WHEREAS, in 1953, he returned to the United States, where he served as professor, spiritual director
and novice master in Scalabrinian seminaries and as associate pastor and pastor in various parishes; and

unflagging commitment to education earned her a term as a trustee of Radcliffe. She was active in the
Harvard & Radcliffe Clubs of Chicago and became one of the first women to serve on the board of
directors of any Harvard Club, and
WHEREAS, Margaret MacGregor Magie loved to entertain with her husband. Her house was often
filled with friends and people working for the many causes she supported, and
WHEREAS, Margaret MacGregor Magie was passionate abo ut gardening. She led the Winnetka
Weeders garden club and cultivated and nurtured the spectacular flower gardens surrou nding her home,

g reat books, and

pass io n for books and learning, community servi ce, faith and devotion, world peace, and love for her
fam il y.

RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE PETER N. SILVESTRI, COUNTY COMMISSIONER

THE HONORABLE JOHN H. STROGER, JR., PRESIDENT, JERRY BUTLER,
ALLAN C. CARR, EARLEAN COLLINS, JOHN P. DALEY, GREGG GOSLIN,

JOSEPH MARIO MORENO, MIKE QUIGLEY, HERBERT T. SCHUMANN, JR.,
DEBORAH SIMS, BOBBIE L. STEELE AND CALVIN R. SUTKER
COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
Designating May 10th as an Annual Peace Officer Day and
Erecting a Monument in Remembrance and Recognition of Peace Officers
in Cook County, Illinois
WHEREAS, according to recently released statistics 15 1 federal , state, and local law enforcement
officers were killed in the line of duty in 2000; and
WHEREAS, such figures represent a 13 per cent increase in the number of peace officers ki lled in the
line of duty from 1999; and

WHEREAS, the National Institute for Occupational Safety and Health has determined that a deputy
sheriff or police officer has the second highest risk of being murdered on the job; and
WHEREAS, such statistics reveal that one police officer is killed somewhere in the United States every
54 hours and that an additional 62,000 assaults are committed against police officers annua lly, resulting in
more than 27,000 injuries; and
WHEREAS, by Act of Congress, May 15th of each year is National Peace Officers Memorial Day, the
first Thursday in May is des ignated as Illinois Police Officer Memorial Day by the state legislature, and
the first Sunday in May is the Chicago Police Department's St. Jude Police League Memorial March; and

1908

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR MAY 15, 200 I

WHEREAS, the nation pays tribute to the fede ral, state, and local law enforcement officers who have
paid the supreme price of their li ves at a National Law Enforcement Officers Memoria l in Washington,
D.C., w ith blue and gray marble walls displaying the names of more than 15,000 offi cers ki lled in the line
of duty since 1792; and
WHEREAS, in 1990, the State of Illinois completed a memorial to honor law enforcement officers who
made the supreme sacrifi ce on behalf of the people of this great state, with a s ix-foot-tall statue of ma le
and female law enforcement officers atop a seven-foot-ta ll, six-sided base; and
WHEREAS, in 2000, the C ity of Chicago dedicated the Gold Star Families Memorial Park along
Chicago's lakefront, with 460 trees planted, o ne hono ring each Chicago police officer killed in the line of
duty; and
WHEREAS, the President and Cook County Board of Commissioners wish to provide a lasting memoria l
to all peace officers killed in the line of duty within our county, whether said officers served as Chicago,
suburban, or county law enforcement agencies, and to pay tribute to those who currently serve in such
positions.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County President and Board of
Commissioners does hereby remember and honor the memories of all peace officers, whether they be
sheriffs, correctional guards, police officers, or any other such service offi cer ki lled in the line of duty,
and do recognize and appreciate the ded ication of those who currently so serve, by designating May I 0th
as Peace Officer Day of Remembrance and Recognitio n in Cook County, Ill inois, beginning in the year
2002, and each year thereafter.
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the Cook County President and Board of Commissio ners does
hereby autho ri ze the Bureau of Ad min istration, with the advice and consent of the Board, to determine an
appropriate location on Cook County property for interested parties to erect a monument in honor of the
men and women who have given the ir lives and who currently serve as law enforcement officers.
Approved and adopted th is 15th day of May 200 I.
JOH N H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DA YID ORR, County Clerk

Comm issioner Sil vestri , seconded by Commissioner Carr, moved to suspend the rules so that this matter
may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.
Commissioner S il vestri, seconded by Commissio ner Daley, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.
